FINDING 1: Phase 1 table count is stated two ways  
Section: §0.2 / §3.2, lines 44 and 177-182  
Severity: important  
Issue: §0.2 says Phase 1 registers “60 currently-unregistered tenant tables” and removes 4 stale entries, while §3.2 says the current gate has 63 unregistered tenant tables plus 4 stale entries, and explicitly says the 60-count drifted. That stale count survived the edit.  
Suggested fix: Change §0.2 to “63 currently-unregistered tenant tables” or avoid the number there and point to §3.4 as the source of truth.

FINDING 2: Phase 1 classification table has no explicit verdicts  
Section: §3.4, lines 202-231  
Severity: critical  
Issue: §3.4 says each row “carries the verdict,” but immediately says verdicts are “not yet filled in,” and §3.4.1 is just a comma-separated table list. That violates the explicit-verdict requirement and leaves implementation scope unresolved before migrations are authored.  
Suggested fix: Replace the comma-separated list with a table containing `Table | Owning migration | Has policy? | Verdict | Notes` and fill every row, or mark Phase 1 as an explicit discovery-only phase and move all policy/registry edits to a later phase after the verdict table exists.

FINDING 3: Files-to-change inventory omits modified files named by the implementation  
Section: §2.2 / §3.5 / §4.3 / §4.8, lines 136-146, 244-251, 338-346, 390  
Severity: critical  
Issue: §4 requires changing `interventionService.recordOutcome` to return a boolean and use `.onConflictDoNothing`, but `server/services/interventionService.ts` is not in §2.2. §3 and §4 also require writing `tasks/builds/pre-prod-tenancy/progress.md`, but that file is not listed in the inventory.  
Suggested fix: Add `server/services/interventionService.ts` and `tasks/builds/pre-prod-tenancy/progress.md` to §2 with phase-specific changes, and include `tasks/todo.md` if the spec expects this branch to write deferral entries.

FINDING 4: Migration batching is internally contradictory  
Section: §2.1 / §3.5 / §6, lines 110, 245-249, 486  
Severity: important  
Issue: §2.1 says “one file per tenant-scoped table” but the same row says migrations are batched up to 4 tables per file. §3.5 and §6 then rely on the batching rule. This leaves the migration inventory ambiguous.  
Suggested fix: Replace “one file per tenant-scoped table” with “one migration file per policy-shape batch, up to 4 canonical tables per file; parent-EXISTS/custom tables get standalone files.”

FINDING 5: Phase 2’s RLS-gate acceptance contradicts Phase 1’s open inventory  
Section: §3.4.1 / §4.8 / §6 / §8.1, lines 216, 394, 485, 553-557  
Severity: important  
Issue: `intervention_outcomes` is listed as one of the unregistered tenant tables in §3.4.1, but §4.8 says the Phase 2 schema change is a no-op for the RLS gate because “the table is already in the registry.” §6 also says Phase 2 can ship before Phase 1, while §4.8 requires `verify-rls-protected-tables.sh` to still exit 0, which cannot be true before Phase 1 closes the registry violations.  
Suggested fix: Either make Phase 2 depend on the Phase 1 registration of `intervention_outcomes`, or add a Phase 2-local requirement to register/policy `intervention_outcomes` before the unique-index acceptance gate.

FINDING 6: Phase 3 changes concurrency semantics but §10 declares no concurrency contract needed  
Section: §5.2 / §5.3 / §10, lines 451-455, 461-463, 616  
Severity: important  
Issue: §5 explicitly says advisory-lock semantics may change and the implementer must decide whether locks protect enumeration or per-org work, but §10 says Phase 3 introduces “no new concurrent-write contests.” That is a load-bearing claim without a per-job enforcement mechanism, especially because moving from one outer admin transaction to multiple `withOrgTx` calls changes lock lifetime.  
Suggested fix: Add a Phase 3 execution-safety subsection naming each job’s lock scope, retry classification, idempotency posture, and losing-run/noop behavior, or defer Phase 3 entirely until that table is authored.

FINDING 7: Load-test acceptance has conflicting pass/fallback language  
Section: §4.7 / §4.8 / §9, lines 374-383, 392, 592  
Severity: minor  
Issue: §4.7 says the 5x speedup “must still be demonstrated” even if the full load test cannot be set up, but §4.8 accepts “≥5x speedup vs. legacy or recorded blocker.” §9 repeats that the absolute number can be deferred, not the 5x comparison. The acceptance criterion therefore allows a blocker where the spec elsewhere says the relative speedup is mandatory.  
Suggested fix: Change §4.8 to require “5x speedup vs. legacy on either the full fixture or named smaller fixture; absolute rows/sec/org may be deferred with a blocker note.”

FINDING 8: `recordOutcome` return contract is not pinned as a concrete signature  
Section: §4.3 / §4.4 / source evidence `server/services/interventionService.ts:53`  
Severity: important  
Issue: The spec uses `const wrote = await interventionService.recordOutcome(...)` and says `recordOutcome` returns true/false, but the current function signature is `Promise<void>` and the spec never gives the replacement signature. That leaves a mechanically important service boundary change implicit.  
Suggested fix: Add the exact new signature in §4.3, e.g. `async recordOutcome(data: RecordOutcomeInput): Promise<boolean>`, and list `RecordOutcomeInput` only if it already exists or is introduced in a named file.
